  1. Risk=High, Confidence=Medium (1)

    1. http://192.168.235.134 (1)

      1. SQL Injection (1)
        1. POST http://192.168.235.134/login.php
          Alert tags
          • POLICY_SEQUENCE =
          • OWASP_2021_A03
          • CWE-89
          • WSTG-v42-INPV-05
          • POLICY_API =
          • POLICY_DEV_FULL =
          • POLICY_QA_STD =
          • POLICY_QA_FULL =
          • OWASP_2017_A01
          • POLICY_DEV_CICD =
          • POLICY_DEV_STD =
          Alert description

          SQL injection may be possible.
          Other info

          The page results were successfully manipulated using the boolean conditions [sYqZABRp AND 1=1 -- ] and [sYqZABRp AND 1=2 -- ]

          The parameter value being modified was stripped from the HTML output for the purposes of the comparison.

          Data was returned for the original parameter.

          The vulnerability was detected by successfully restricting the data originally returned, by manipulating the parameter.
          Request
          Request line and header section (540 bytes) 
          POST http://192.168.235.134/login.php HTTP/1.1
host: 192.168.235.134
User-Agent: Mozilla/5.0 (X11; Linux x86_64; rv:128.0) Gecko/20100101 Firefox/128.0
Accept: text/html,application/xhtml+xml,application/xml;q=0.9,*/*;q=0.8
Accept-Language: en-US,en;q=0.5
Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded
content-length: 53

Connection: keep-alive

Priority: u=0, i
          Request body (53 bytes) 
          username=sYqZABRp+AND+1%3D1+--+&password=&Login=Login
          Response
          Status line and header section (471 bytes) 
          HTTP/1.1 302 Found
Date: Mon, 24 Mar 2025 11:27:04 GMT
Server: Apache/2.2.14 (Unix) DAV/2 mod_ssl/2.2.14 OpenSSL/0.9.8l PHP/5.3.1 mod_apreq2-20090110/2.7.1 mod_perl/2.0.4 Perl/v5.10.1
X-Powered-By: PHP/5.3.1
Expires: Thu, 19 Nov 1981 08:52:00 GMT
Cache-Control: no-store, no-cache, must-revalidate, post-check=0, pre-check=0
Pragma: no-cache
Location: login.php
Content-Length: 0
Keep-Alive: timeout=5, max=91
Connection: Keep-Alive
Content-Type: text/html
          Response body (0 bytes)
          Parameter 
          username
          Attack 
          sYqZABRp AND 1=1 --
          Solution

          Do not trust client side input, even if there is client side validation in place.

          In general, type check all data on the server side.

          If the application uses JDBC, use PreparedStatement or CallableStatement, with parameters passed by '?'

          If the application uses ASP, use ADO Command Objects with strong type checking and parameterized queries.

          If database Stored Procedures can be used, use them.

          Do *not* concatenate strings into queries in the stored procedure, or use 'exec', 'exec immediate', or equivalent functionality!

          Do not create dynamic SQL queries using simple string concatenation.

          Escape all data received from the client.

          Apply an 'allow list' of allowed characters, or a 'deny list' of disallowed characters in user input.

          Apply the principle of least privilege by using the least privileged database user possible.

          In particular, avoid using the 'sa' or 'db-owner' database users. This does not eliminate SQL injection, but minimizes its impact.

          Grant the minimum database access that is necessary for the application.

      1. Content Security Policy (CSP) Header Not Set (1)
        1. GET http://192.168.235.134/
          Alert tags
          • CWE-693
          • OWASP_2021_A05
          • OWASP_2017_A06
          Alert description

          Content Security Policy (CSP) is an added layer of security that helps to detect and mitigate certain types of attacks, including Cross Site Scripting (XSS) and data injection attacks. These attacks are used for everything from data theft to site defacement or distribution of malware. CSP provides a set of standard HTTP headers that allow website owners to declare approved sources of content that browsers should be allowed to load on that page â€” covered types are JavaScript, CSS, HTML frames, fonts, images and embeddable objects such as Java applets, ActiveX, audio and video files.

  3. Risk=Medium, Confidence=Medium (4)

    1. http://192.168.235.131:3000 (1)

      1. Cross-Domain Misconfiguration (1)
        1. GET http://192.168.235.131:3000/rest/products/24/reviews
          Alert tags
          • OWASP_2017_A05
          • CWE-264
          • OWASP_2021_A01
          Alert description

          Web browser data loading may be possible, due to a Cross Origin Resource Sharing (CORS) misconfiguration on the web server.
          Other info

          The CORS misconfiguration on the web server permits cross-domain read requests from arbitrary third party domains, using unauthenticated APIs on this domain. Web browser implementations do not permit arbitrary third parties to read the response from authenticated APIs, however. This reduces the risk somewhat. This misconfiguration could be used by an attacker to access data that is available in an unauthenticated manner, but which uses some other form of security, such as IP address white-listing.

          Solution

          Ensure that sensitive data is not available in an unauthenticated manner (using IP address white-listing, for instance).

          Configure the "Access-Control-Allow-Origin" HTTP header to a more restrictive set of domains, or remove all CORS headers entirely, to allow the web browser to enforce the Same Origin Policy (SOP) in a more restrictive manner.

          Parameter 
          x-frame-options
          Solution

          Modern Web browsers support the Content-Security-Policy and X-Frame-Options HTTP headers. Ensure one of them is set on all web pages returned by your site/app.

          If you expect the page to be framed only by pages on your server (e.g. it's part of a FRAMESET) then you'll want to use SAMEORIGIN, otherwise if you never expect the page to be framed, you should use DENY. Alternatively consider implementing Content Security Policy's "frame-ancestors" directive.

<dl><dt><a name="mod_proxy.c"><strong>Module Name:</strong></a> <font size="+1"><tt><a href="?mod_proxy.c">mod_proxy.c</a></tt></font></dt>
<dt><strong>Content handlers:</strong> <tt> <em>yes</em></tt></dt><dt><strong>Configuration Phase Participation:</strong>
<tt>Create Directory Config</tt>, <tt>Merge Directory Configs</tt>, <tt>Create Server Config</tt>, <tt>Merge Server Configs</tt></dt><dt><strong>Request Phase Participation:</strong>
<tt>Post-Read Request</tt>, <tt>Translate Name</tt>, <tt>Map to Storage</tt>, <tt>Fixups</tt>, <tt>Content Handlers</tt></dt>
<dt><strong>Module Directives:</strong></dt><dd><tt>&lt;Proxy&gt; - <i>Container for directives affecting resources located in the proxied location</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>&lt;ProxyMatch&gt; - <i>Container for directives affecting resources located in the proxied location, in regular expression syntax</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyRequests - <i>on if the true proxy requests should be accepted</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyRemote - <i>a scheme, partial URL or '*' and a proxy server</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyRemoteMatch - <i>a regex pattern and a proxy server</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassInterpolateEnv - <i>Interpolate Env Vars in reverse Proxy</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPass - <i>a virtual path and a URL</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassMatch - <i>a virtual path and a URL</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassReverse - <i>a virtual path and a URL for reverse proxy behaviour</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassReverseCookiePath - <i>Path rewrite rule for proxying cookies</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassReverseCookieDomain - <i>Domain rewrite rule for proxying cookies</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyBlock - <i>A list of names, hosts or domains to which the proxy will not connect</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyReceiveBufferSize - <i>Receive buffer size for outgoing HTTP and FTP connections in bytes</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyIOBufferSize - <i>IO buffer size for outgoing HTTP and FTP connections in bytes</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyMaxForwards - <i>The maximum number of proxies a request may be forwarded through.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>NoProxy - <i>A list of domains, hosts, or subnets to which the proxy will connect directly</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyDomain - <i>The default intranet domain name (in absence of a domain in the URL)</i></tt></dd>

<dl><dt><a name="mod_authnz_ldap.c"><strong>Module Name:</strong></a> <font size="+1"><tt><a href="?mod_authnz_ldap.c">mod_authnz_ldap.c</a></tt></font></dt>
<dt><strong>Content handlers:</strong> <tt> <em>none</em></tt></dt><dt><strong>Configuration Phase Participation:</strong>
<tt>Create Directory Config</tt></dt><dt><strong>Request Phase Participation:</strong>
<tt>Verify User Access</tt></dt>
<dt><strong>Module Directives:</strong></dt><dd><tt>AuthLDAPURL - <i>URL to define LDAP connection. This should be an RFC 2255 complaint
URL of the form ldap://host[:port]/basedn[?attrib[?scope[?filter]]].
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Host is the name of the LDAP server. Use a space separated list of hosts 
to specify redundant servers.
&lt;li&gt;Port is optional, and specifies the port to connect to.
&lt;li&gt;basedn specifies the base DN to start searches from
&lt;li&gt;Attrib specifies what attribute to search for in the directory. If not provided, it defaults to &lt;b&gt;uid&lt;/b&gt;.
&lt;li&gt;Scope is the scope of the search, and can be either &lt;b&gt;sub&lt;/b&gt; or &lt;b&gt;one&lt;/b&gt;. If not provided, the default is &lt;b&gt;sub&lt;/b&gt;.
&lt;li&gt;Filter is a filter to use in the search. If not provided, defaults to &lt;b&gt;(objectClass=*)&lt;/b&gt;.
&lt;/ul&gt;
Searches are performed using the attribute and the filter combined. For example, assume that the
LDAP URL is &lt;b&gt;ldap://ldap.airius.com/ou=People, o=Airius?uid?sub?(posixid=*)&lt;/b&gt;. Searches will
be done using the filter &lt;b&gt;(&amp;((posixid=*))(uid=&lt;i&gt;username&lt;/i&gt;))&lt;/b&gt;, where &lt;i&gt;username&lt;/i&gt;
is the user name passed by the HTTP client. The search will be a subtree search on the branch &lt;b&gt;ou=People, o=Airius&lt;/b&gt;.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPBindDN - <i>DN to use to bind to LDAP server. If not provided, will do an anonymous bind.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPBindPassword - <i>Password to use to bind to LDAP server. If not provided, will do an anonymous bind.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPRemoteUserIsDN - <i>Set to 'on' to set the REMOTE_USER environment variable to be the full DN of the remote user. By default, this is set to off, meaning that the REMOTE_USER variable will contain whatever value the remote user sent.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPRemoteUserAttribute - <i>Override the user supplied username and place the contents of this attribute in the REMOTE_USER environment variable.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthzLDAPAuthoritative - <i>Set to 'off' to allow access control to be passed along to lower modules if the UserID and/or group is not known to this module</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPCompareDNOnServer - <i>Set to 'on' to force auth_ldap to do DN compares (for the &quot;require dn&quot; directive) using the server, and set it 'off' to do the compares locally (at the expense of possible false matches). See the documentation for a complete description of this option.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPGroupAttribute - <i>A list of attributes used to define group membership - defaults to member and uniquemember</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPGroupAttributeIsDN - <i>If set to 'on', auth_ldap uses the DN that is retrieved from the server forsubsequent group comparisons. If set to 'off', auth_ldap uses the stringprovided by the client directly. Defaults to 'on'.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPDereferenceAliases - <i>Determines how aliases are handled during a search. Can bo one of thevalues &quot;never&quot;, &quot;searching&quot;, &quot;finding&quot;, or &quot;always&quot;. Defaults to always.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPCharsetConfig - <i>Character set conversion configuration file. If omitted, character setconversion is disabled.</i></tt></dd>

      5. Server Leaks Information via "X-Powered-By" HTTP Response Header Field(s) (1)

Access to such information may facilitate attackers identifying other frameworks/components your web application is reliant upon and the vulnerabilities such components may be subject to.

      6. X-Content-Type-Options Header Missing (1)
        1. GET http://192.168.235.134/
          Alert tags
          • CWE-693
          • OWASP_2021_A05
          • OWASP_2017_A06
          Alert description

          The Anti-MIME-Sniffing header X-Content-Type-Options was not set to 'nosniff'. This allows older versions of Internet Explorer and Chrome to perform MIME-sniffing on the response body, potentially causing the response body to be interpreted and displayed as a content type other than the declared content type. Current (early 2014) and legacy versions of Firefox will use the declared content type (if one is set), rather than performing MIME-sniffing.
          Other info

          This issue still applies to error type pages (401, 403, 500, etc.) as those pages are often still affected by injection issues, in which case there is still concern for browsers sniffing pages away from their actual content type.

          At "High" threshold this scan rule will not alert on client or server error responses.
          Request
          Request line and header section (386 bytes) 
          GET http://192.168.235.134/ HTTP/1.1
host: 192.168.235.134
User-Agent: Mozilla/5.0 (X11; Linux x86_64; rv:128.0) Gecko/20100101 Firefox/128.0
Accept: text/html,application/xhtml+xml,application/xml;q=0.9,*/*;q=0.8

		<p>Damn Vulnerable Web App is damn vulnerable! Do not upload it to your hosting provider's public html folder or any internet facing web server as it will be compromised. <dd><tt>&lt;ProxyMatch&gt; - <i>Container for directives affecting resources located in the proxied location, in regular expression syntax</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyRequests - <i>on if the true proxy requests should be accepted</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyRemote - <i>a scheme, partial URL or '*' and a proxy server</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyRemoteMatch - <i>a regex pattern and a proxy server</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassInterpolateEnv - <i>Interpolate Env Vars in reverse Proxy</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPass - <i>a virtual path and a URL</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassMatch - <i>a virtual path and a URL</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassReverse - <i>a virtual path and a URL for reverse proxy behaviour</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassReverseCookiePath - <i>Path rewrite rule for proxying cookies</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPassReverseCookieDomain - <i>Domain rewrite rule for proxying cookies</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyBlock - <i>A list of names, hosts or domains to which the proxy will not connect</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyReceiveBufferSize - <i>Receive buffer size for outgoing HTTP and FTP connections in bytes</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyIOBufferSize - <i>IO buffer size for outgoing HTTP and FTP connections in bytes</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyMaxForwards - <i>The maximum number of proxies a request may be forwarded through.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>NoProxy - <i>A list of domains, hosts, or subnets to which the proxy will connect directly</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyDomain - <i>The default intranet domain name (in absence of a domain in the URL)</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AllowCONNECT - <i>A list of ports which CONNECT may connect to</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyVia - <i>Configure Via: proxy header header to one of: on | off | block | full</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyErrorOverride - <i>use our error handling pages instead of the servers' we are proxying</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyPreserveHost - <i>on if we should preserve host header while proxying</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyTimeout - <i>Set the timeout (in seconds) for a proxied connection. This overrides the server timeout</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyBadHeader - <i>How to handle bad header line in response: IsError | Ignore | StartBody</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>BalancerMember - <i>A balancer name and scheme with list of params</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyStatus - <i>Configure Status: proxy status to one of: on | off | full</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxySet - <i>A balancer or worker name with list of params</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>ProxyFtpDirCharset - <i>Define the character set for proxied FTP listings</i></tt></dd>

<dl><dt><a name="mod_authnz_ldap.c"><strong>Module Name:</strong></a> <font size="+1"><tt><a href="?mod_authnz_ldap.c">mod_authnz_ldap.c</a></tt></font></dt>
<dt><strong>Content handlers:</strong> <tt> <em>none</em></tt></dt><dt><strong>Configuration Phase Participation:</strong>
<tt>Create Directory Config</tt></dt><dt><strong>Request Phase Participation:</strong>
<tt>Verify User Access</tt></dt>
<dt><strong>Module Directives:</strong></dt><dd><tt>AuthLDAPURL - <i>URL to define LDAP connection. This should be an RFC 2255 complaint
URL of the form ldap://host[:port]/basedn[?attrib[?scope[?filter]]].
&lt;ul&gt;
&lt;li&gt;Host is the name of the LDAP server. Use a space separated list of hosts 
to specify redundant servers.
&lt;li&gt;Port is optional, and specifies the port to connect to.
&lt;li&gt;basedn specifies the base DN to start searches from
&lt;li&gt;Attrib specifies what attribute to search for in the directory. If not provided, it defaults to &lt;b&gt;uid&lt;/b&gt;.
&lt;li&gt;Scope is the scope of the search, and can be either &lt;b&gt;sub&lt;/b&gt; or &lt;b&gt;one&lt;/b&gt;. If not provided, the default is &lt;b&gt;sub&lt;/b&gt;.
&lt;li&gt;Filter is a filter to use in the search. If not provided, defaults to &lt;b&gt;(objectClass=*)&lt;/b&gt;.
&lt;/ul&gt;
Searches are performed using the attribute and the filter combined. For example, assume that the
LDAP URL is &lt;b&gt;ldap://ldap.airius.com/ou=People, o=Airius?uid?sub?(posixid=*)&lt;/b&gt;. Searches will
be done using the filter &lt;b&gt;(&amp;((posixid=*))(uid=&lt;i&gt;username&lt;/i&gt;))&lt;/b&gt;, where &lt;i&gt;username&lt;/i&gt;
is the user name passed by the HTTP client. The search will be a subtree search on the branch &lt;b&gt;ou=People, o=Airius&lt;/b&gt;.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPBindDN - <i>DN to use to bind to LDAP server. If not provided, will do an anonymous bind.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPBindPassword - <i>Password to use to bind to LDAP server. If not provided, will do an anonymous bind.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPRemoteUserIsDN - <i>Set to 'on' to set the REMOTE_USER environment variable to be the full DN of the remote user. By default, this is set to off, meaning that the REMOTE_USER variable will contain whatever value the remote user sent.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPRemoteUserAttribute - <i>Override the user supplied username and place the contents of this attribute in the REMOTE_USER environment variable.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthzLDAPAuthoritative - <i>Set to 'off' to allow access control to be passed along to lower modules if the UserID and/or group is not known to this module</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPCompareDNOnServer - <i>Set to 'on' to force auth_ldap to do DN compares (for the &quot;require dn&quot; directive) using the server, and set it 'off' to do the compares locally (at the expense of possible false matches). See the documentation for a complete description of this option.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPGroupAttribute - <i>A list of attributes used to define group membership - defaults to member and uniquemember</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPGroupAttributeIsDN - <i>If set to 'on', auth_ldap uses the DN that is retrieved from the server forsubsequent group comparisons. If set to 'off', auth_ldap uses the stringprovided by the client directly. Defaults to 'on'.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPDereferenceAliases - <i>Determines how aliases are handled during a search. Can bo one of thevalues &quot;never&quot;, &quot;searching&quot;, &quot;finding&quot;, or &quot;always&quot;. Defaults to always.</i></tt></dd>
<dd><tt>AuthLDAPCharsetConfig - <i>Character set conversion configuration file. If omitted, character setconversion is disabled.</i></tt></dd>
